<li>Explain factors that affect the antigen antibody reactions</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-1-principle-of-antigen-antibody-interactions">6.1 Principle of Antigen Antibody Interactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-1-principle-of-antigen-antibody-interactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the field of immunology, many serologic techniques are used to detect the interaction of antigens with antibodies. These methods are suitable for the detection and quantitation of antibodies to infectious agents, as well as microbial and non-microbial antigens.</p>
<p>In antigen antibody interaction determination of either antigen or antibody is possible, this determination follows a general principle: know antigen suspension or antiserum is used to detect and measure unknown antibody or microbial antigen.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-in-vitro-antigen-antibody-reactions-and-their-role-in-the-diagnosis-of-disease">6.2 In Vitro Antigen Antibody Reactions and Their Role in the Diagnosis of Disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-in-vitro-antigen-antibody-reactions-and-their-role-in-the-diagnosis-of-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>There are different types of antigen antibody interaction these include</p>
<ul>
<li>Precipitation reaction</li>
<li>Agglutination reaction</li>
<li>Complement fixation reaction</li>
<li>Enzyme Immuno Assay (EIA)</li>
<li>Radio Immuno Assay (RIA)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-1-precipitation-reaction">6.2.1 Precipitation Reaction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-1-precipitation-reaction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Precipitins can be produced against most proteins and some carbohydrates and carbohydrates- lipid complexes. Various system are available in which precipitation tests are performed in semisolid media such as agar or agarose, or nongel support medium such as cellulose acetate. Agar has been found to interfere with the migration of charged particles and has been largely replaced as an immunodiffusion medium by agarose. Agarose is a transparent, colorless, neutral gel. In the clinical laboratory several applications of the precipitation reaction are used. These methods include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Immunodiffusion</li>
<li>Electroimmunodiffusion</li>
</ul>
<p>56</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Immunodiffusion: These are of two type: single and double immuodiffusion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="i-double-diffusion">I. Double diffusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#i-double-diffusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This technique also referred to as the Ouchterlony method, may be used to determine the relation ship between antigen and antibodies.</p>
<p><strong>Principle:</strong> Antibody dilutions and specific soluble antigens are placed in adjacent wells. If the well size and shape, distance between wells, temperature, and incubation time are optimal, these solutions diffuse out, bind to each other, cross-link, and form a visible precipitate at the point of equivalence perpendicular to the axis line between the wells. The precipitation bands will be compared with a standard antigen.</p>
<p>The precise location of the band depends on the concentration and rate of diffusion of antigen and antibody. In a condition of antibody excess, the band will be located nearer the antigen well. If two antigens are present in the solution that can be recognized by the antibody, two precipitin bands form independently.</p>
<p>Antibodies associated with autoimmune disorders such as rheumatoid arthritis and systemic lupus erythematosus can be identified by double diffusion.</p>
<p>57</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="identity">Identity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>An identity reaction is indicated when the precipitin band forms a single smooth area. This precipitin is formed between the antibody and the two test antigens fuses (figure 6-1A), indicating that the antibody is precipitating identical antigen specificities in each preparation. This does not mean that the antigens are necessarily identical; they are only identical insofar as the antibody can distinguish the difference.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-47fccec5.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-1bfd5696.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-5fdb4f27.jpeg" alt="img-15.jpeg">
Figure 6-1</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-d958c8e6.jpeg" alt="img-16.jpeg"></p>
<p>Precipitation pattern of ouchterlony type of immunodiffusion.</p>
<p>(From Mary LT: Immunology and serology in laboratory medicine,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>2</mn><mtext>nd</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2^{\text{nd}}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">nd</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> ed,st Louis, 1996,Mosby)</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="nonidentity">Nonidentity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nonidentity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A non-identity pattern (Fig 6-1B) is expressed when the precipitation line cross each other. They intersect or cross because the sample contain no antigenic determinants in common.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="partial-identity">Partial Identity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#partial-identity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In a partial identity pattern (Fig 6-1C), the precipitation lines merge with spur formation. This merger indicated that the antigen are non identical but possess common determinants.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="ii-single-radial-immunodiffusion">II. Single radial immunodiffusion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#ii-single-radial-immunodiffusion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is a simple and specific method for identification and quantitation of a number of proteins found in human serum and other body fluids.</p>
<p><strong>Principle:</strong> Radial immunodiffusion is based on a technique using a precipitin reaction in which specific antibody is added to a buffered agarose medium, serum containing the test antigen is placed in a well centered in the agarose. The diameter of the resulting precipitin zone is related to the concentration of antigen placed in a well.</p>
<p>59</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-0aee4714.jpeg" alt="img-17.jpeg">
Figure 6.2 single radial immunodiffusion.</p>
<p>The unknown antigen is in the wells and the specific antibody in the agar, the greater the antigen concentration the larger the circle of precipitation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="eletroimmuno-diffusion-eid">Eletroimmuno diffusion (EID)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#eletroimmuno-diffusion-eid" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>EID is a variation of the double immunodiffusion reaction in a support medium such as cellulose acetate or agarose through the use of an electric current that enhances the mobility of reactants and increase their movement towards each other.</p>
<p>Antibody is placed in the well favoring its migration in the direction of the cathode; antigens that tend to be more negatively charged and placed in the well that favors migration of the anode. Precipitin bands form at a point of equivalence in a shorter periods of time.</p>
<p>Electro immunodiffusion method, like immunodiffusion procedures, are classified into one-or-two-dimensional, singles, or double diffusion when a voltage is applied across</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>the gels to move the antigens and antibodies together, immuno-double diffusion becomes counter current immuno electrophoresis (CIE) radial immunodiffusion (RID) becomes electro immunoassay (EIA).</p>
<p>Counter Current immunoelectrophoresis (CIE) is a variation of the classic precipitin procedure; it merely adds an electrical current to help antigens and antibodies move towards each other more quickly than in simple diffusion. The procedure takes advantage of the net electric charge of the antigens and antibodies being tested in a particular test buffer. Variables such as types of gel, amount of current, a concentration of antigen and antibody must be carefully controlled for maximum reactivity. The sensitivity of CIE is 10 to 20 times greater than in immuno-double diffusion; however, it is more expensive than other techniques such as immunodiffusion</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="electro-immunoassay">Electro immunoassay<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#electro-immunoassay" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Antigens may be quantitated by electrophoresis than in an antibody-containing gel electroimmunoassay. This technique combines the speed of electrophoresis with the accuracy and sensitivity of radioimmunoassay.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-2-agglutination-reaction">6.2.2 Agglutination Reaction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-2-agglutination-reaction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Precipitation and agglutination are the visible expression of the aggregation of antigens and antibodies through the formation of a framework in which antigen particles or molecules alternate with antibody molecules.</p>
<p>Agglutination of particles to which soluble antigen has been absorbed produces a serum method of demonstrating precipitins. Example of artificial carriers includes latex particles and colloidal charcoal. Cells unrelated to the antigen, such as erythrocytes coated with antigen in a constant amount can be used as a biologic carriers. Whole bacterial cells can contain an antigen that will bind with antibodies produced in response to that antigen when it was introduced into the host.</p>
<p>Agglutination tests are easy to perform and in some cases are the most sensitive tests currently available. These tests have a wide range of applications in the clinical diagnosis of noninfectious immune disorders and infectious diseases.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="latex-agglutination">Latex agglutination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#latex-agglutination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In latex agglutination procedures, antibody molecules can be bound to the surface of latex beads. Many antibody molecules can be bound to each latex particle, increasing the potential</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>number of exposed antigen-binding sites. If an antigen is present in a test specimen, the antigen will bind to the combining sites of the antibody exposed on the surface of the latex heads, forming visible cross-linked aggregates of latex beads and antigen. In some test systems, latex particles can be coated with antigen. In the presence of serum antibodies, these particles agglutinate in to large visible clumps.</p>
<p>Examples of tests based on latex agglutination reaction include C-reactive protein, IgG rheumatoid factors, and IgM rheumatoid factors.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-a24febcb.jpeg" alt="img-18.jpeg">
Figure 6.3 Latex agglutination reaction</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="direct-bacterial-agglutination">Direct bacterial agglutination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-bacterial-agglutination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Direct whole pathogens can be used to detect antibodies directed against pathogens. The most basic tests are those that measure the antibody produced by the host to determinants on the surface of a bacterial agent in response to infection with that bacterium. In a thick suspension of the bacteria, the binding of specific antibodies to surface antigens of the bacteria causes the bacteria to clump together in visible aggregates. This type agglutination is called bacterial agglutination. Because tube testing allows more time for antigen-antibody reaction, it is considered to be more sensitive than slide testing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="indirect-or-passive-hemagglutination">Indirect or passive hemagglutination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indirect-or-passive-hemagglutination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Hemagglutination is agglutination of red blood cells, and tests for antibody detection. In the indirect or passive hemagglutination technique, erythrocytes are coated with substances such as extracts of bacterial cells, protozoa or purified polysaccharides or proteins.</p>
<p>Erythrocyte of animals such as sheep or rabbits, or from group "O" humans, function as carrier for detecting and titrating the corresponding antibodies by agglutination. This technique is called indirect or passive hemagglutination testing because it is not the antigen of the erythrocytes</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>themselves but the passively attached antigens that are bound by antibody. For example, in rubella antibody test, erythrocytes are coated with rubella antigen. In the presence of antibody, agglutination occurs.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="hemagglutination-inhibition-technique">Hemagglutination Inhibition technique<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#hemagglutination-inhibition-technique" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Hemagglutination inhibition test is used to detect some viral antibodies, for example, rubella. A known quantity of rubella viral antigen is mixed with dilutions of the patient's serum, to which red blood cells are added. If the serum lacks antibody, the virus will spontaneously attach to the red cells, link together, and agglutinate. If antibody to the virus is present, all of the virus particles will be bound by antibody, which prevents or inhibits hemagglutination. The serum is therefore positive for the antibodies. The highest dilution of serum that totally inhibits agglutination of red cells determines the antibody titer of the serum.</p>
<p>Disadvantage of this technique include: time consuming, &amp; subjective bias in the interpretation for results. Negative results do not always indicate the absence of antibody. In some case false negative results can occur from a low titer of antibody. Nonspecific inhibitors can cause false positive results.</p>
<p>65</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-2-3-complement-fixation-reaction">6.2.3 Complement Fixation Reaction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-3-complement-fixation-reaction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Complement fixation is a classic method for demonstrating the presence of antibody in serum. This method consists of two components. The first component is an indicator system consisting of a combination of sheep red cells; complement-fixing antibody produced against the sheep red cells in another animal, and an exogenous source of complement, usually guinea pig serum. When these three components are combined in an optimal concentration, the antisheep cell antibody, hemolysin, can bind to the surface of the red cells. Complement can subsequently bind to this antigen antibody complex and cause cell lysis. The second component consists of a known antigen and patient serum, which are added to a suspension of sheep erythrocytes, hemolysin, and a complement.</p>
<p>The two components of the complement fixation procedure are tested in sequence. Patient serum is first added to the known antigen, and complement is added to the solution. If the serum contains antibody to the antigen, the resulting antigen antibody complexes will bind all of the complement. Sheep red cells and hemolysin are then added. If complement has not been bound by an antigen antibody complex formed from the patient serum and known antigen, it is available to bind to the indicator system of indicates both a lack of</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>antibody and a negative complement fixation test. If the patient's serum does contain a complement fixing antibody apposite result will be demonstrated by the lack of haemolysis.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-b7e513f1.jpeg" alt="img-19.jpeg">
Figure 6.4 complement fixation test</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="6-2-4-immunofluorescent-test-ift">6.2.4 Immunofluorescent Test (IFT)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-4-immunofluorescent-test-ift" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The fluorescent techniques are extremely specific and sensitive. This technique consists of labeling antibody with fluorescein isothiocyanate, a fluorescent compound with an affinity for proteins to form a complex, conjugate. The</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>fluorescent assay includes: direct immunofluorescent assay and indirect immunofluorescent assay.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="direct-immunofluorescent-assay">Direct Immunofluorescent assay<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#direct-immunofluorescent-assay" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In this technique, Fluorescein-conjugated antibody is used to detect antigen-antibody reactions. This method can be applied to the detection of hepatitis B virus &amp; chlamydia. A fluorescent microscope is required to observe the production of color; fluorescein gives a yellow- green light.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="indirect-immunofluorescent-assay-ifa">Indirect Immunofluorescent Assay (IFA)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#indirect-immunofluorescent-assay-ifa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This method is based on the fact that antibodies not only react with homologous antigens but can act as antigens and react with antibody.</p>
<p>In the indirect immunofluorescent assay, the antigen source to the specific antibody being tested is fixed to the surface of a microscopic slide. The patent's serum is diluted and placed on the slide to cover the antigen source. If antibody is present in the serum, it will bind to its specific antigen unbound antibody is then removed by washing the slide, finally antihuman globulin conjugated to a fluorescent substance that will fluoresce when exposed to a fluorescent substance that will fluoresce when exposed to ultraviolet light is placed on the slide. This conjugated marker of human antibody will bind to the antibody already bound to the antigen on the slide and will</p>
<p>68</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>serve as a marker for the antibody when viewed under a fluorescent microscope.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-5-enzyme-immuno-assay-eia">6.2.5 Enzyme Immuno Assay (EIA)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-5-enzyme-immuno-assay-eia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>An enzyme labeled antibody or enzyme labeled antigen conjugate is used in immunologic assays for detection of antigens or antibodies, in a patient's serum e.g. HIV antibody, HIV antigen, hepatitis A antibody.</p>
<p>Various enzymes are employed in enzyme immunoassay. The most commonly used enzymes are peroxidase and alkaline phosphatase. In EIA, a plastic bead or plastic plate is coated with antigen. The antigen reacts with antibody in the patient serum. The bead or plate is then incubated with an enzyme-labeled antibody conjugate, if antibody is present on the bead or plate. The enzyme activity is measured spectrophotometrically after the addition of the specific chromogenic substrate. Test result is calculated by comparing the spectrophotometer reading of patient serum to that of a control serum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-2-6-radio-immunoassay-ria">6.2.6 Radio Immunoassay (RIA)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-2-6-radio-immunoassay-ria" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In radioimmunoassay, radioisotopes can be used to measure the concentration of antigen or antibody in serum sample. If</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>antibody concentration is being measured, radioactive labeled antibody competes with patient unlabeled antibody for binding sites on a known amount of antigen.</p>
<p>The main advantage of the radioimmunoassay method is the extreme sensitivity and ability to detect trace amounts. Of antigen or antibody. In addition, a large number of tests can be performed in a relatively short time period. The disadvantage is the hazards and instability of isotopes.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="6-3-factors-affecting-antigen-antibody-reactions">6.3 Factors Affecting Antigen Antibody Reactions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#6-3-factors-affecting-antigen-antibody-reactions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Many factors affect the interaction between antigen and antibody; these include specificity, cross reactivity, temperature PH, ionic strength, concentration, and intermolecular specificity.</p>
<p><strong>Specificity</strong>: The ability of a particular antibody to combine with one antigen instead of another is referred to as specificity. This property resides in the portion of the antigen-binding fragment of an immunoglobulin molecule. Antigen-antibody reactions can show a high level of specificity. Specificity exists when the binding sites of antibodies directed against determinants of one antigen.</p>
<p>70</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Cross reactivity: When some of the determinants of an antigen are shared by similar antigenic determinants on the surface apparently unrelated molecules, a proportion of the antibodies directed against one kind of antigen will also react with the other kind of antigen. This is called cross reactivity. Antibodies directed against a protein in one species may also react in a detectable manner with the homologous protein in another species, which is another example of cross reactivity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="example-of-cross-reactivity">Example of cross reactivity<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#example-of-cross-reactivity" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Three organisms might possess antigenic structures and produce corresponding antibodies as follows:</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Organism</th><th>Antigens</th><th>Antibodies</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>1</td><td>ABC</td><td>abc</td></tr><tr><td>2</td><td>BCD</td><td>bcd</td></tr><tr><td>3</td><td>DE</td><td>de</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Antiserum prepared from organism 1 will react with organism 1&amp;2 antiserum prepared from organism 2 will react with 1,2, &amp;3 antiserum produced from organism 3 will react organism 2&amp;3 but not with organism1.</p>
<p>Temperature: The optimum temperature needed to reach equilibrium in an antibody-antigen reaction differs for different antibodies. Igm antibodies are cold reacting with thermal</p>
<p>71</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>range 4-22°C, and IgG antibodies are warm reacting, with an optimum temperature of reaction at 37°C.</p>
<p>pH: Although the optimum pH for all reactions has not been determined, a pH of 7.0 is used for routine laboratory testing.</p>
<p>Ionic strength: The concentration of salt in the reaction medium has an effect on antibody uptake by the membrane bound erythrocyte antigens. Sodium and chloride ions in solution have inhibition effect. These ions cluster around and partially neutralize the opposite charges on antigen and antibody molecules, which hinders the association of antibody with antigen. Reducing or lowering the ionic strength of a reaction medium such as low-ionic strength salt can enhance antibody uptake.</p>
<p>Concentration: Under normal condition the concentration of antigen and antibody should be optimal but some time this thing fail to be happen in which excess antibody or antigen concentration will result in false reaction, some times known as zonal reaction. When the concentration of antigen is excess it is known as post zone reaction; excess antibody is referred as prozone reaction. This phenomenon can by overcome by serial dilution until optimum amount of antigen and antibody will present.</p>
<p>72</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="bond-strength-and-inter-molecular-attractive-force">Bond strength and inter molecular attractive force<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#bond-strength-and-inter-molecular-attractive-force" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Bonding of an antigen to an antibody takes place because of the formation of multiple, reversible, intermolecular attraction between an antigen and amino acids of the binding site. The bonding of antigen to antibody is exclusively non covalent. The attractive force of noncovalent bonds is weak when compared to covalent bonds, but the formation of multiple non covalent bonds produces considerable total- binding energy. The strength of a single antigen- antibody bond is termed antibody affinity.</p>
<p>The strongest bonding develops when antigens and antibodies are close to each other and when the shapes of both the antigenic determinate and the antigen-binding site conform to each other. This complementary matching is referred to as goodness of fit.</p>
<p>73</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-questions">Review Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="serological-techniques">SEROLOGICAL TECHNIQUES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#serological-techniques" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objectives">Learning Objectives<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objectives" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<ul>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-1-materials-necessary-for-basic-serologic-tests">7.1 Materials Necessary for Basic Serologic Tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-1-materials-necessary-for-basic-serologic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>As discussed in the previous chapter, wide verities of serologic techniques are available to detect either an antibody or antigen. For the detection of this unknown substance from patient's specimen, the specimen should be collected and prepared appropriately. In addition the equipment that is used for testing should be free from any contaminants so as to get true result. The following are some of the equipment used in routine serology.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="glasswares">Glasswares<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glasswares" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Dirty glasswares easily affect serological test. After using all the glass wares (test tube, beaker, pipette, etc.) they should be socked in detergent for several hours and rinsed several times in tap water. Finally allow drying by placing in a dry oven or dust free place. Test tubes and pipettes should not be scratched or broken, which will interfere with the reading of a test.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="types-of-glassware-include">Types of glassware include:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#types-of-glassware-include" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Test tube</li>
<li>Glass slides</li>
<li>Serologic pipette with a size of 10ml, 5ml, 2ml&amp;1ml.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="constant-temperature-device">Constant temperature device<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#constant-temperature-device" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Incubator and water bath are usually used in serologic tests. These materials are electrically operated and have thermostat that hold the temperature within the required limits. These devices should be checked prior to use by installing a thermometer</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="rotating-machines">Rotating machines<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rotating-machines" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rotating machines are required to facilitate antigen antibody reactions. Such machine has a flat plate, which rotate at a prescribed rate of speed. A knob located on the front part of the machine controls the number of revolution per minute.</p>
<p>76</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-2-collection-preparation-and-preservation-of-specimen-for-serologic-tests">7.2 Collection Preparation and Preservation of Specimen for Serologic Tests<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-2-collection-preparation-and-preservation-of-specimen-for-serologic-tests" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Specimens that are used for serologic test include: serum, plasma &amp; cerebrospinal fluid. Serum or plasma sample could be obtained from venous blood, which can be performed by the laboratory personnel however. Cerebrospinal fluid should be collected by a physician or a trained nurse.</p>
<p>For serum or plasma sample, first 2-3 ml of venous blood is collected using sterile syringe and needle from a patient. If serum is required, allow the whole blood to clot at room temperature for at least one hour and centrifuge the clotted blood for 10 minutes at 2000 rpm. Then transfer the serum to a labeled tube with a pasture pipette and rubber bulb.</p>
<p>Plasma sample is obtained by treating fresh blood with an anticoagulant, centrifuge and separate the supernatant.</p>
<p>The specimen should be free from hemolyzed blood. Finally, seal the specimen containing tube; the tube should be labeled with full patient's identification (Age, Sex, code n°, etc). The test should be performed with in hours after sample collection, if this could not be done preserve it at -20°C.</p>
<p>77</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-3-shipment-of-serological-specimen">7.3 Shipment of Serological Specimen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-3-shipment-of-serological-specimen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Most health center and clinic laboratories often are limited in the diagnostic procedures that can be carried out and have to ship serologic specimens to other laboratories. Before shipment the following things should be considered.</p>
<ul>
<li>Don't ship whole blood unless the tests to be performed require whole blood.</li>
<li>Do not inactivate serum or plasma before mailing.</li>
<li>Keep the specimen and packing container in the refrigerator until time of shipment but if shipment requires several days, freeze the specimen.</li>
<li>Then ship the specimen by the fastest route.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="7-4-complement-inactivation">7.4 Complement Inactivation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-4-complement-inactivation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Complement inactivation is important because it is known to interfere with different tests. In activation of complement can be achieved by heating the serum or plasma at 56°C for 30 minutes. If more than four hours has elapsed since inactivation, a specimen should be re-inactivated with same temperature 10 minutes.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-5-serial-dilution">7.5 Serial Dilution<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-5-serial-dilution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Dilution is the act of making a weaker solution from a stronger one. This is usually done by adding a water or saline, which contains none of the material being diluted. Dilution is usually expressed as one unit of the original solution to the total number of units of final solution. Serial dilution means decreasing the volume of serum progressively by maintaining a constant volume of fluid most commonly, serial dilutions are two fold, that is, each dilution is half as concentrated as the preceding one. The total volume in each tube is the same.</p>
<p>Table 7.1. An example of serial dilution</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Tube no</th><th>1</th><th>2</th><th>3</th><th>4</th><th>5</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Saline (ml)</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>1</td><td>1</td></tr><tr><td>Patient serum (ml)</td><td>1</td><td>1 of 1: 2</td><td>1 of 1: 4</td><td>1 of 1: 8</td><td>1 of 1: 16</td></tr><tr><td>Final dilution</td><td>1:2</td><td>1:4</td><td>1:8</td><td>1:16</td><td>1:32</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="7-6-determination-of-endpoint-and-titer">7.6 Determination of Endpoint and Titer<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#7-6-determination-of-endpoint-and-titer" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>If we take the above example again, after serially diluting the patient's serum, equal amount of an antigen is added in each dilution to observe immunologic reaction. The last tube that shows visible immunologic reaction is known as end point of</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>the test, the dilution of the antiserum at the end point is known as the titer. The reciprocal of the greatest reacting dilution of the serum is considered as the measure of titer or the concentration of the antibody. For example, it the highest dilution of the serum that shows a visible reaction is at 1:32 dilution, the titer of the test is expressed as 32.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-293c58eb.jpeg" alt="img-21.jpeg"></p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-questions">Review Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

</ol>

<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-eight">CHAPTER EIGHT<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-eight" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="syphilis-serology">SYPHILIS SEROLOGY<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#syphilis-serology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objective">Learning Objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the end of this chapter, the learner should be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Enumerate the different treponematoses</li>
<li>Explain the stages of syphilis</li>
<li>Practice collection of specimen from lesion</li>
<li>Practice the different tests for syphilis</li>
<li>Practice preparation of control sera in the laboratory</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-1-treponematoses">8.1 Treponematoses<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-1-treponematoses" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is a chronic inflammatory disease, primarily it affects the skin and mucous membrane, and during latent period other organs and tissues may be affected. Medically important species is mainly T. palladium but there are other pathogenic treponemes like T. pertenue, T. endemicum &amp; T. carateum.</p>
<p>Each of these organisms are obligate parasite of humans, morphologically identical, cannot be cultured in vitro and have similar laboratory diagnosis and treatment.</p>
<p>These diseases differ in there:</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ul>
<li>Geographical distribution,</li>
<li>pathogenicity and</li>
<li>degree of virulence.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="t-pertenue">T. pertenue<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#t-pertenue" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cause a disease known as yaws. Its geographical distribution is West Africa, central Africa south East Asia. T.pertenue is transmitted through exposed skin. Hand, face, legs and feet are parts of the body most affected, it produce raised granular papilloma on the skin. In the later stage, disfigurement of the infected area will be resulted.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="t-endemicum">T. endemicum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#t-endemicum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cause endemic syphilis. It is widely distributed in sub-Saharan Africa and transmitted through exposed skin and oral mucosa.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="t-carateum">T.carateum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#t-carateum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Cause a disease pinta, has geographical distribution of central and South America, transmitted through exposed skin. The organisms produce itchy red papules on the uncovered part of the body. In the later stage when infected area healed loss of the normal pigment will be resulted.</p>
<p>83</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-2-syphilis">8.2 Syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-2-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Syphilis is caused by a spirochete bacterium, Treponema pallidum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-2-1-morphology-and-metabolism-of-t-pallidum">8.2.1 Morphology and Metabolism of T. Pallidum<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-2-1-morphology-and-metabolism-of-t-pallidum" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Microscopically T. pallidum appears as fine, spiral (8 to 24 coils) organism, approximately 6-15 µm long.</p>
<p>They are not cultivatable with any consistency in artificial laboratory media out side the host. T. pallidum are extremely susceptible to a variety of physical and chemical agents. However, they may remain viable for up to 5 days in tissue specimens removed from diseased animals and from frozen specimens.</p>
<p>Syphilis is a venereal disease. It can be acquired by kissing a person with active oral lesion. There are very few cases of transfusion-acquired syphilis. In addition, syphilis may be transmitted transplacentally to the fetus. Spirochetes can be transmitted to the fetus during the last trimester of pregnancy.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-2-2-stages-of-syphilis">8.2.2 Stages of Syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-2-2-stages-of-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Untreated syphilis is a chronic disease with sub acute symptomatic periods separated by asymptomatic intervals, during which the diagnosis can be made serologically.</p>
<p>The progression of untreated syphilis is generally divided in to stages. Initially, T.pallidum penetrates intact mucous membranes or enters the body through tiny defects in the epithelium. Upon entrance, the microorganism is carried by the circulatory system to every organ of the body. Spirochetemia occurs very early in infection, even before the first lesions have appeared or blood tests become reactive. Before chemical or serologic manifestations develop patients are said to be 'incubating syphilis'. The incubation period usually lasts about 3 weeks but can range from 10-90 days.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="primary-syphilis">Primary syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#primary-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the end of the incubation period, a patient develops a characteristics primary inflammatory lesion called a chancre at the point of initial inoculation and multiplication of the spirochetes. The chancre begins as a papule and erodes to form a gradually enlarging ulcer with a clean base and indurate edge. Generally it is relatively painless and commonly located around the genitalia, but in about 10% of</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>cases lesions may appear almost any where else on the body e.g. Throat, lip, hands.</p>
<p>Most of the patients with primary syphilis will develop swelling of inguinal lymph nods. The primary chancre will persist for 1 to 5 weeks and will heal completely within about 4 to 6 weeks. Primary syphilis is diagnosed by its characteristics chancre with positive serological test and detection of T.pallidum by dark field examination from the lesion.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="secondary-syphilis">Secondary syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#secondary-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Within 2 to 8 weeks after the appearance of the primary chancre, a patient may develop the sign and symptoms of secondary syphilis when organisms gain access to the circulation from the infected site.</p>
<p>The secondary stage is characterized by a generalized illness that usually begins with symptoms suggesting a viral infection headache, sore throat, low-grade fever and occasionally nasal discharges. Blood tests reveal a moderate increase in leukocytes with a relative increase in lymphocytes.</p>
<p>The disease progresses with the development of lymhadenopathy and lesions of the skin and mucous membranes corresponding to the spread of the organism in the body by way of the circulating blood. The lesions contain a</p>
<p>86</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>large number of spirochetes, and when located on exposed surfaces, are highly contagious. Macular lesions are common, and a rash invariably involves the genitalia and of ten is prominent on the palms and soles.</p>
<p>Secondary syphilis usually resolves it self within 2 to 6 weeks, even in the absence of therapy. It may be diagnosed by typical skin rash and positive syphilis serology test.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="latent-syphilis">Latent syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#latent-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>After resolution of untreated secondary syphilis, the patient enters a latent non-infectious state in which diagnosis can be made only by serologic method. During the first 2-4 years of infection, one fourth of patients will show relapses of manifestation of secondary syphilis. During these relapses, patients are infectious, and the underlying spirochetemia may be passed translucently to the fetus.</p>
<p>Relapses are extremely rare after four years of latency. About one third of patients entering latency are eventually spontaneously cured of the disease, one third will never develop further clinical manifestation of the disease and the remaining one third will eventually develop late syphilis.</p>
<p>87</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="late-tertiary-syphilis">Late (Tertiary) syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#late-tertiary-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The first manifestations of late syphilis are usually seen from 3-10 years after primary infection. About 15% of untreated syphilitic individuals eventually develop late benign syphilis characterized by the presence of destructive granulomas.</p>
<p>These granulomas, or gummas, may produce lesions resembling segments of circles that often heal with superficial scarring. Treponems are rarely found in the lesions, which are referred to as benign gummas.</p>
<p>Of untreated patients 10% develop cardiovascular manifestations. T. pallidum may damage large blood vessels such as aorta and coronary arthritis. This condition is usually fatal.</p>
<p>In about 8% of untreated patients, late syphilis involves the CNS. Initially CNS disease is asymptomatic and can be detected only by examination of cerebrospinal fluid. In symptomatic neurosyphilis, spirochetes may also involve the brain tissue and cause destructions of the brain parenchyma (paresis), dorsal root of the spinal cord (tabes).</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="congenital-syphilis">Congenital syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#congenital-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Congenital syphilis is caused by maternal spirochetemia and transplacental transmission of the microorganism usually after</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>18 weeks of gestation. Congenital syphilis is diagnosed in three fourths of the cases in patients over 10 years of age. About half of damage to the fetus depends on the stage of the disease and the number of treponemes circulating in pregnant women at the time of transmission.</p>
<p>Early congenital syphilis appears either at birth or up to two years of age, the manifestation includes cutaneous lesion, mucous membrane lesion like thick nasal discharge containing T.pallidum.</p>
<p>Late congenital syphilis may be characterized by fissuring around the mouth, anus, skeletal lesions, and perforation of the palate and the collapse of nasal bones to produce a saddle-nose deformity.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-2-3-antibodies-in-syphilis">8.2.3 Antibodies in Syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-2-3-antibodies-in-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the treponemes, two classes of antigen have been recognized those restricted to one or a few species and those shared by many different spirochetes. Infection with T.pallidum, T.pertenue, T.carateum T.endemicum produces similar antibody response. Specific and non-specific antibodies are produced in the immunocompetent host.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="specific-antibody">Specific antibody<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specific-antibody" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Antibodies in early or untreated early latent syphilis are predominantly IgM antibodies. The early immune response to infection is rapidly followed by the appearance of IgG antibodies. The greatest elevation in IgG concentration is seen in secondary syphilis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="non-specific-nontreponemal-or-reagin-antibodies">Non - specific (nontreponemal or reagin) antibodies<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#non-specific-nontreponemal-or-reagin-antibodies" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Are produced by infected patients against components of their own or other mammalian cells. Reagin is widespread in nature and can be isolated from any mammalian tissues as well as from treponemes. Although patients with syphilis almost always produce these antibodies, patients with other infectious disease, like measles, hepatitis, leprosy, Brucelosis, malaria, rickettsia, also produce them. Patients can also exhibit reagin with non-infectious conditions such as drug addition, old age, pregnancy and recent immunization.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-2-4-collection-and-handling-of-syphilitic-specimen-from-lesion">8.2.4 Collection and Handling of Syphilitic Specimen from Lesion<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-2-4-collection-and-handling-of-syphilitic-specimen-from-lesion" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The treponemal lesion is infectious. As a result wearing a rubber glove is vital to protect one self from infection. The following procedure should be followed to get a representative sample. Cleanse the area of chancre with swab moistened</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>with physiological saline. Apply gentle pressure on the area to squeeze the sample from the depth of the lesion. Collect the sample of serous exudates on a cover glass and invert it on a slide. Deliver immediately the preparation to the laboratory for examination by dark-field microscopy.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="8-3-tests-for-syphilis">8.3 Tests for Syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-3-tests-for-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Either demonstration of microorganism in a lesion or serologic testing confirms the clinical diagnosis of syphilis in the laboratory. The serologic methods for syphilis measure the presence of two types of antibodies: treponemal and non treponemal.</p>
<p>Serologic procedures for syphilis include the following.</p>
<ol>
<li>Nontreponemal method e.g. Venereal Disease research laboratory (VDRL) and the rapid plasma regain (RPR) procedures.</li>
<li>Treponemal methods e.g. Fluorescent Treponema pallidum antibody absorption (FTA-ABS) and microhemagglutination Treponema pallidum MHA-TP).</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nontreponemal-methods">Nontreponemal methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nontreponemal-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The VDRL and RPR are the two most widely used nontreponemal serologic procedures. Each is a flocculation or agglutination test in which soluble antigen particles coalesce</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>to form larger particles visible as clumps when they are aggregated by antibodies.</p>
<p>The VDRL procedure is recommended when a patient suspected of having syphilis has a negative dark field microscopy result or when atypical lesions are present. It is further recommended that a quantitative VDRL assessment be made quarterly for 1 year after treatment for syphilis, or that the adequacy of treatment in both early and latent syphilis be monitored. The VDRL procedure can be performed on cerebrospinal fluid for the detection of neurosyphilis.</p>
<p>The RPR test can be performed on unheated serum or plasma using a modified VDRL antigen suspension of choline chloride with EDTA. The RPR test card test antigen also contains charcoal for macroscopic reading. It is about as specific as, and possibly more sensitive than, the VDRL slide test.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="treponemal-methods">Treponemal methods<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#treponemal-methods" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The FTA – ABS and MHA represent treponemal methods. Reactive (Positive) regain test can be confirmed with these two specific treponemal antigen tests. These procedures, however, should not be used as primary screening methods. Procedures such as the FTA-ABS and MHA can be used to confirm that a positive non-treponemal test result has been</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>caused by syphilis rather than one of the other biologic conditions that can produce positive VDRL, or they can determine quantitative titer of antibody, which is useful in following response to therapy.</p>
<p>The FTA-Abs uses a killed suspension of T. pallidum spirochetes as the antigen.</p>
<p>The micro hemagglutination assay for T. pallidum is based on agglutination by specific antibodies in the patient's serum with sheep erythrocytes sensitized to T. pallidum antigen. The Treponema pallidum immobilization test (TPI) method is obsolete.</p>
