<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sensitivity-of-commonly-used-serologic-tests-for-syphilis">Sensitivity of commonly used serologic tests for syphilis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sensitivity-of-commonly-used-serologic-tests-for-syphilis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Detection of syphilis by serologic methods is related both to the stage of the disease and to the test method. In the primary stage, about 30% of cases become serologically active after one week and 90% of patients demonstrate reactivity after three weeks. Reagin titers increase rapidly during the first four weeks of infection and then remain stationary for approximately six months. Patients in the secondary stage of syphilis are serologically positive. During latent syphilis there is a gradual return of non-reactive serologic manifestations with non-treponemal method. About one third of patients in the latent stage will remain seroreactive and presumably</p>
<p>93</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>infectious. In late syphilis, treponemal tests are generally reactive, non-treponemal methods are non reactive.</p>
<p>Table 8.1 Sensitivity of commonly used serologic tests for syphilis</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Test</th><th></th><th>Stage</th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td></td><td>Primary</td><td>Secondary</td><td>Late</td></tr><tr><td>Non treponemal (regain tests)</td><td>70%</td><td>99%</td><td>1% (treated late syphilis)</td></tr><tr><td>VDRL</td><td>80%</td><td>99%</td><td>0%</td></tr><tr><td>RPR</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Specific treponemal tests</td><td>85%</td><td>100%</td><td>95%</td></tr><tr><td>FTA-ABS</td><td>65%</td><td>100%</td><td>95%</td></tr><tr><td>TPHA-TP</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>Treponema pallidium Immobilization (TPI)</td><td>50%</td><td>97%</td><td>95%</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="8-3-1-venereal-disease-research-laboratory-vdrl-qualitative-slide-test">8.3.1 Venereal Disease Research Laboratory (VDRL) Qualitative Slide Test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-3-1-venereal-disease-research-laboratory-vdrl-qualitative-slide-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Principle: heat inactivated serum is mixed with a buffered saline suspension of cardiolipin-lecithin-cholesterol antigen. This serum-antigen mixture is microscopically examined for flocculation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specimen-collection-and-preparation">Specimen collection and preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specimen-collection-and-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>The specimen should include all identification, it must include the patient's full name, the date the specimen is collected and the patient's hospital identification number.</p>
<p>Blood should be drawn by an aseptic technique. The required specimen is a minimum of 2 ml of clotted blood. The specimen should be promptly centrifuged and an aliquot of the serum removed. Severely lipemic or hemolyzed serum is unsuitable for testing. Before testing, the serum must be heat in activated at  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>56</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">56^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">6</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  for 30 minutes. In activated serum should be reheated at  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>56</mn><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">∘</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">56^{\circ}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6741em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">6</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.6741em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">∘</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>  for 10 minutes if tested more than 4 hours after the original in activation. Cerebrospinal fluid is also an appropriate fluid for testing.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reagents-required">Reagents required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagents-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>VDRL antigen - a colorless, alcoholic solution containing  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.03</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.03\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">0.03%</span></span></span></span></span>  cardiolipin,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.9</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.9\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">0.9%</span></span></span></span></span>  cholesterol, and sufficient purified</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>lecithin to produce standard reactivity. Each lot must be serologically standardized by comparison with an antigen of know reactivity. Ampules should be stored in the dark at either at 6C° to 10 C° or at room temperature antigen that contains precipitate should be discarded.</p>
<p>VDRL- buffered saline</p>
<p>Contains 1% sodium chloride, PH 6.0 ± 0.1, it should be stored in screw capped or glass stopper bottles</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="equipment-required">Equipment required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equipment-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>VDRL test slide with paraffin of ceramic ring.</li>
<li>18 gauges hypodermic needle with out bevel (it will deliver 60 drops) ml of reagents.</li>
<li>30 ml flat-bottomed glass with stopper, narrow mouth bottle</li>
<li>Syringe (1-2ml)</li>
<li>Rotator</li>
<li>Serological graduated pipette</li>
<li>Water bath 56°C</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-working-antigen-suspension">Preparation of working antigen suspension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-working-antigen-suspension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Dispense 0.4 ml of buffered saline to the bottom of the 30ml, round, glass-stopper bottle.</li>
<li>Rapidly add 0.5ml of antigen drop by drop directly by rotating the bottle in a circular motion on a flat surface.</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>The pipette tip should remain in upper third of the bottle. Take care to avoid splashing saline on the pipette. Blow the last drop of antigen from the pipette without touching the pipette to the saline.</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Continue to rotate the bottle for 10 seconds.</li>
<li>Add 4.1 ml of buffered saline with a 5 ml pipette</li>
<li>Place the stopper on the bottle and shake up and down approximately 30 times in 10 seconds. The antigen suspension is ready for use, but it must be gently mixed at the time of use. Do not force back and forth through the needle &amp; syringe as this may lead to break down of antigen particles and loss of their activity.</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: The working antigen suspension can be stabilized by adding 50 µl of benzoic acid to 5ml of the diluted working solution instead of discarding within 24 hours. The temperature of the buffer saline and antigen should be in the range of 23° to 29C°. The antigen suspension must be used on the day of preparation.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="quality-control">Quality control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#quality-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Include positive control sera of graded reactivity each time serologic testing is performed. The antigen suspension to be used each day is first examined with these control sera. Store control sera frozen at -20°C or liquid form for 7 to 10 days.</p>
<p>97</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Thaw, mix thoroughly, and heat in activate at 56°C before use.</p>
<p>Check antigen – dispensing needle at the time of use to be sure that it accurately deliver 60-drops/ml reagents. Clean needles and syringes by rinsing with water, alcohol and acetone. Remove needle from syringe after cleaning.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Pipette 0.5 ml of inactivated patient serum in to one of the rings of the ceramic-ringed slide. Pipette additional specimen and controls in to additional rings.</li>
<li>Add one drop of antigen suspension to each serum with a calibrated 18-gauge needle and syringe held in a vertical position.</li>
<li>Rotate the slide on a mechanical rotator for 4 minutes. In externally dry climate, cover the slide with a lid containing moistened filter paper to prevent evaporation during rotation.</li>
<li>Examine each specimen microscopically with the low (10x) objective.</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> The test should be performed at a temperature range of 23°-29°C.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reporting-results">Reporting Results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reporting-results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Non reactive: No clumping or very slight roughness weakly reactive: Small clumps</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Reactive: medium and large clumps</p>
<p>Weakly reactive: small clumps</p>
<p>Note: All reactive and weakly reactive specimens (sera) should be tested quantitatively to estimate the antibody titer. False negative reactions it can occur in a variety of situations like:</p>
<ul>
<li>Technical error (e.g. unsatisfactory antigen preparation or techniques.
The presence of inhibitors in the patient's serum</li>
<li>Low antibody titer patients may have syphilis, but the reagin concentration is too low to produce a reactive test result. It may be caused by several factors: an infection that is too recent to have produced antibodies, the effect of treatment, latent or inactive disease, or patients who have not produced protective antibodies because of immunological tolerance. These seronegative patients may demonstrate a positive reaction with more sensitive treponemal tests such as the FTA-ABS.</li>
</ul>
<p>Inappropriate temperature</p>
<ul>
<li>Prozone reaction</li>
</ul>
<p>Weakly reactive results can be caused by</p>
<ul>
<li>Very early infection</li>
<li>Lessening of the activity of the disease after treatment.</li>
<li>Improper technique or questionable reagents</li>
</ul>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>False - positive reactions can also be observed. Of all positive serologic tests for syphilis,  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>10</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">10\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">10%</span></span></span></span></span>  to  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>30</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">30\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">30%</span></span></span></span></span>  may be false biologic positive reactions. Non-syphilitic positive VDRL reactions have been reported with cardiolipin type of antigen in rheumatic fever, pneumococcal pneumonia, infectious hepatitis, leprosy, malaria, pregnancy, aging individuals, rheumatoid arthritis. Contaminated or hemolyzed specimens can also produce false positive results.</p>
<p>LIMITATIONS: The VDRL procedure is not specific for syphilis but may demonstrate positive reactions in other reagin-producing disorders, infectious disease and alterations such as pregnancy or aging in normal physiology.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="vdrl-quantitative-test">VDRL quantitative test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vdrl-quantitative-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Principle: Retest quantitatively to an end-point titer all sera that produce reactive, weakly reactive, or questionably non-reactive results in the qualitative VDRL slide test.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="specimen-collection-and-preparation">Specimen collection and preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specimen-collection-and-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Same as VDRL Qualitative test for undiluted serum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="preparation-of-serial-dilution">Preparation of serial dilution.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-serial-dilution" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>A. Pipette  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.05</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.05\mathrm{ml}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6944em;"></span><span class="mord">0.05</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">ml</span></span></span></span></span></span>  of  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.9</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.9\%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">0.9%</span></span></span></span></span>  saline in to ring number 2,3 &amp;4 on ceramic slide do not spread the saline.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Serum 1-</th><th>1</th><th>2</th><th>3</th><th>4</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td></td><td>1:1</td><td>1:2</td><td>1:4</td><td>1:8</td></tr><tr><td>Serum 2 -</td><td>1</td><td>2</td><td>3</td><td>4</td></tr><tr><td>---</td><td>---</td><td>---</td><td>---</td><td>---</td></tr><tr><td></td><td>1:1</td><td>1:2</td><td>1:4</td><td>1:8</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>B. Pipette 0.05 ml of serum to ring numbers 1 and 2. Draw the serum and saline mixture up and down in the pipette tip in ring number 2 to mix. Aspirate 0.05 ml of diluted serum and spread the remaining dilution over the entire area of the circle with the pipette tip.</p>
<p>C. Transfer 0.05ml of the diluted (1:2) serum in ring number 2 to ring number 3. Draw the serum and saline mixture. Aspirate 0.05 ml of diluted serum and spread the remaining dilution over the entire area of the circle with the pipette tip.</p>
<p>D. Transfer 0.05 ml of the diluted (1:4) serum in ring number 3 to ring number 4 Draw the serum and saline mixture up and down in the pipette tip in ring number 3 to mix. Aspirate 0.05 ml of diluted serum and spread the remaining dilution over the entire area of the circle with the pipette tip.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>E. Discard 0.05 ml of the diluted (1:8) serum from ring number 4 unless greater dilutions are needed for strongly relative serum, and spread the remaining dilution over the entire area of the circle with the pipette tip.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reagent-supplies-and-equipment">Reagent, Supplies, and equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagent-supplies-and-equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In addition to the VDRL qualitative test the following reagent and piece of equipment are needed.</p>
<ul>
<li>0.9% saline</li>
</ul>
<p>Preparation – weigh 0.9gm of sodium chloride to a left volumetric flask. Dilute to the calibration mark with distilled water</p>
<ul>
<li>Safety pipette (50ml or 0.05ml)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Add one drop of antigen suspension to each diluted serum with a calibrated 18-gauge needle and syringe held in a vertical position.</li>
<li>Rotate the slide on a mechanical rotator for 4 minutes.</li>
<li>Examine each specimen microscopically (10x objective)</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: the test should be performed at a temperature range of 23° to 29°C.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reporting-results">Reporting results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reporting-results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Report the titer in terms of the highest dilution that produces a reactive (weakly reactive) result.</p>
<p>Example:</p>
<p>Serum Dilutions Result</p>
<p>1:1 1:2 1:4 1:8</p>
<p>Reactive Reactive Weakly Non Reactive, 1:4</p>
<p>reactive reactive dilution or 4</p>
<p>dilutions</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-3-2-rapid-plasma-reagin-rpr-card-test">8.3.2 Rapid Plasma Reagin (RPR) Card Test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-3-2-rapid-plasma-reagin-rpr-card-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="principle">Principle<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#principle" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>A cardiolipin lecithin-cholesterol antigen coated with carbon particle is mixed with patient's serum. Then flocculation reaction is observed macroscopically in the presence of cardiolipin antigen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="specimen-collection-and-preparation">Specimen collection and preparation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#specimen-collection-and-preparation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>No special preparation is required before specimen collection. The specimen should be labeled with all patient's identification fresh serum or plasma sample can be used. It is not important to heat inactivate the specimen before testing.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="reagents-equipment">Reagents &amp; Equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagents-equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Note: Except for the antigen, all other components should be stored at room temperature in a dry place in the original kit packaging.</p>
<p>Provided in the test kit</p>
<p>RPR card test antigen</p>
<p>It contains cardiolipin, lecithin, cholesterol, EDTA, charcoal, chorine chloride, and distilled water. Store the antigen suspension in ampules or in plastic dispensing bottle at <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>2</mn><mn>0</mn></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2^{0}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8141em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>8</mn><mn>0</mn></msup><mi mathvariant="normal">C</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">8^{0}\mathrm{C}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8141em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">8</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8141em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">0</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span class="mord mathrm">C</span></span></span></span></span>. Unopened ampules have a shelf life of 12 months from the date of manufacture.</p>
<p>Opened antigen ampules has stability for 3 months</p>
<ul>
<li>Needle, 18-gauge, without bevel. The needle should deliver <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>60</mn><mo>±</mo><mn>2</mn></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">60 \pm 2</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">60</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">±</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.6444em;"></span><span class="mord">2</span></span></span></span></span> drops of antigen suspension per milliliter when held in a vertical position.</li>
<li>Specially prepared, plastic-coated cards</li>
<li>Serological pipette</li>
<li>Dispenser, 0.05 ml/drop</li>
<li>Stirrer</li>
</ul>
<p>Other material</p>
<ul>
<li>Rotator</li>
<li>Humidifier cover containing a moistened sponge</li>
<li>0.9% saline</li>
</ul>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="quality-control">Quality control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#quality-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A. Controls with established patterns of graded reactivity should be included in each day's testing to confirm optimal reactivity of the antigen suspension. Control sera must be at 23° to 29°C at the time of testing.</p>
<p>B. Calibrate the delivery needle before testing</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Place 0.05ml of unheated serum on the test card with a serologic pipette. Don't touch card surface.</li>
<li>Spread serum in the circle with stirrer</li>
<li>Gently shake antigen-dispensing bottle before use. Hold the needle in a vertical position; dispense exactly one free-falling drop (1/60 ml). Do not stir. Mixing is accomplished during rotation.</li>
<li>Place card on rotator and cover with humidifier cover. The card can be hand rocked and used where laboratory equipment is not available.</li>
<li>Rotate 8 minutes at 100 rpm on mechanical rotator.</li>
<li>Observe the specimen immediately</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reporting-results">Reporting results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reporting-results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Reactive: slight to large agglutination (black clumps)</p>
<p>Non-reactive: no agglutination, or very slight roughness (even light – gray color).</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="sources-of-error">Sources of error<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#sources-of-error" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Error can be introduced in to test results because of factor such as contamination of rubber bulbs or improperly prepared antigen suspension.</li>
<li>Biological false positive occur in the following conditions like rheumatic fever, viral pneumonia, hepatitis, leprosy, malaria, pregnancy, aging individuals.</li>
<li>False negative reaction can result from poor technique, in ineffective reagents or improper rotation.</li>
<li>If mechanical rotation is below or above the 95 to 110 rpm (acceptable range) there is a tendency for the clumping of antigen to be less intense in procedures with undiluted specimen, so that some minimal reactions may be missed.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-3-3-fluorescent-treponema-pallidum-antibody-absorption-test">8.3.3 Fluorescent Treponema Pallidum Antibody Absorption Test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-3-3-fluorescent-treponema-pallidum-antibody-absorption-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Principle: Patients serum is added on the slide coated with T. pallidum antigen followed by addition of fluorescent-tagged anti-human globulin and examine under fluorescent microscope. It's the most sensitive confirmatory test</p>
<p>Specimen collection and preparation</p>
<p>The serum should be heat inactivated</p>
<p>The specimen should be labeled with all the identification</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reagent-supplied">Reagent supplied<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagent-supplied" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Treponema pallidum antigen: Extracted from rabbit testicular tissue</p>
<p>Store at 6°C - 10°C in lyophilized form</p>
<p>Conjugate (fluorescent labeled anti-human globulin)</p>
<p>Positive control</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="equipment">Equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Test tubes, pipette</li>
<li>Incubator</li>
<li>Fluorescent microscope</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Coat the slide with T.pallidum antigen by adding a drop of suspension of T.pallidum on a clean slide and keep in oven at low temperature</li>
<li>Take out and wash by rinsing with tap water to remove excess unbounded T.pallidum</li>
<li>Add the patient's serum to the coated antigen and incubate, rinse by tap water to remove excess antibody, if the pt serum has an antibody, and to remove the whole serum if it doesn't contain antibody.</li>
<li>Add conjugate (fluorescent tagged antihuman globulin) and rinse with tap water, to remove excess conjugate, if</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>serum contain antibody and to remove the whole conjugate, if it doesn't contain antibody.</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Examine under fluorescent microscope.
The fluorochromes usually used are</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>Fluorescein isothyocyanate – yellow green</li>
<li>Rudamin - Red color</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reporting-results">Reporting results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reporting-results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Fluorescence indicate the presence of specific antibody to T.pallidum
Non – fluorescence indicate the absence of specific antibody to T.pallidum.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="8-3-4-preparation-of-control-sera">8.3.4 Preparation of Control Sera<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#8-3-4-preparation-of-control-sera" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Collect all reactive sera and store in freezer</li>
<li>Collect all non reactive sera and store in freezer</li>
<li>After collecting a large amount thaw at room temperature</li>
<li>Filter to remove the particles</li>
<li>Add mertiolet (preservative) 1 mg/ml serum.</li>
<li>Make a serial dilution of reactive with non reactive sera</li>
<li>Perform several tests each day. Select the dilution, which always gives reactive, weakly reactive and non-reactive result.</li>
<li>Prepare a large quantities of those dilution</li>
</ol>
<p>108</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ol start="9">
<li>Distribute in a small container (alginate) and store in a freezer.</li>
<li>Control sera of graded reactivity should be included each time when serologic procedures are performed.</li>
</ol>
<p>NB: If the control sera fail to give the desired (known) result (do not produce the established relativity) pattern the result of the specimen is unacceptable so to have acceptable result the following should be done:</p>
<ul>
<li>Prepare another antigen suspension</li>
<li>Test temperature must be adjusted at room temperature (23-29°C)</li>
<li>Adjust equipment</li>
<li>Use commercially prepared controls</li>
<li>Strictly follow the manufactures procedure.</li>
</ul>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-questions">Review Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Discuss the different stages of syphilis</li>
<li>Explain how specimen is collected from lesion of syphilitic patients</li>
<li>Discuss the difference between treponemal and non treponemal tests for syphilis</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-89791ec8.jpeg" alt="img-23.jpeg"></p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chapter-nine">CHAPTER NINE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chapter-nine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="agglutination-test-for-febrile-disease">AGGLUTINATION TEST FOR FEBRILE DISEASE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#agglutination-test-for-febrile-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objective">Learning Objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>At the end of this chapter, the learner should be able to:</p>
<ul>
<li>Explain the etiology and way of transmission of febrile disease</li>
<li>Practice widal and Weil-felix tests</li>
</ul>
<p>When any pathogenic microorganism invades the human body, the natural response is the production of antibodies. The host and microbial factors influence the rate of antibody formation, the type and amount of antibodies produced, and the persistence of antibody in the circulation. Among the antibodies produced in response to certain pathogenic microorganism are febrile agglutinins. The microorganism that elicits the production of febrile agglutinin is characterized by presence of persistent fever &amp; frequently difficult to grow in laboratory cultures. Some of the causative agents of febrile diseases are salmonella species, rickettsial and brucella abortus.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-1-typhoid-and-paratyphoid-fever">9.1 Typhoid and Paratyphoid Fever<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-1-typhoid-and-paratyphoid-fever" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>The etiological agent is Salmonella species; it occurs in human only. Some times it is termed as enteric fever since they colonize the intestine. Salmonella of medically important species are S.typhi (typhoid fever), S.paratyphi A and B (paratyphoid fever).</p>
<p>Typhoid and paratyphoid fever is transmitted through ingestion of contaminated food or water. They contaminate usually by carriers like rodents, hens, cows, etc. Typhoid or enteric fever is a clinical syndrome characterized by fever, headache, splenomegaly, leucopenia &amp; cough.</p>
<p>Its incubation period ranges from 7 to 14 days. In 5% to 10% of untreated patients relapse may occur the symptoms in relapse are milder than the initial illness and begin about two weeks after discontinuation of antimicrobial therapy. The carrier state is asymptomatic and in 1 - 3% of carriers there is continuous excretion of S.typhi for a minimum of one year. The gall bladder is the site of persistent intestinal infection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="identification-of-salmonella">Identification of salmonella<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#identification-of-salmonella" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Salmonella species can be identified based on their antigenic structure they possess. They have three different antigenic structures.</p>
<p>112</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="o-antigen-somatic-antigen">O- antigen (somatic antigen)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#o-antigen-somatic-antigen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>It is lipopolysaccharide of the outer membrane, which is heat and alcohol stable antigen. Salmonella is divided in to five distinct serogroups (A-E) on the basis of somatic antigen.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="h-antigen-flagellar-antigen">H-antigen (flagellar antigen)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#h-antigen-flagellar-antigen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>H-antigen is protein, which makes the perithrichous flagella. It is heat and alcohol labile. Salmonella is further subdivided in to more than 1200 serotypes on the basis of flagellar antigens.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="vi-antigen">Vi- Antigen:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#vi-antigen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>This is the antigen that determines the virulence, the ability to cause disease, of the organism.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="preparation-of-antigen-suspension">Preparation of antigen suspension<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#preparation-of-antigen-suspension" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Salmonella antigen suspension is available commercially and it's also possible to prepare in the laboratory.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-preparation-of-h-antigen-flagellar-antigen">A. Preparation of H antigen (flagellar antigen)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-preparation-of-h-antigen-flagellar-antigen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Inoculate bacteria from a single colony in to a broth and incubate for 6hrs.</li>
<li>View a drop of the culture in a wet film to confirm that most of the bacteria are motile and therefore sufficiently flagellated for the tests.</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ol start="3">
<li>Kill the culture by adding formaldehyde to a concentration of 0.2% and incubate for several hours at 37°C</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="b-preparation-of-o-antigen">B. Preparation of O antigen<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-preparation-of-o-antigen" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Suspend the bacteria from an agar culture in saline and heat for 30 minute at 100°C to remove the flagella.</li>
<li>Centrifuge to separate the bacteria from the detached flagella.</li>
<li>Resuspend the bacteria in saline.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="alternatively">Alternatively<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#alternatively" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Remove the flagella by mixing a dense saline suspension of the bacteria with an equal volume of absolute ethanol</li>
<li>Incubate for 20 hr at 37°C</li>
<li>Dilute the suspension with saline.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="widal-test">Widal test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#widal-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p>Widal test is a serological test, which is commonly used to diagnose typhoid and paratyphoid fever. The patient's serum is tested for O and H antibodies</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="rapid-slide-screening-test">Rapid slide (Screening) test<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rapid-slide-screening-test" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Clean the glass slides supplied in the kit well and wipe it free of water.</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Place one drop of undiluted test serum in each of the first circle (1to4) and one drop of positive control serum in each of the last two circles.</li>
<li>Place one drop of antigen O, H, A (H) and B (H) in circle 1,2,3, &amp;4 respectively and O antigen in circle five and H antigen in circle 6</li>
<li>Mix the contents of each circle with separate applicator stick and spread to fill the whole area of the individual circle.</li>
<li>Rotate the slide for one minute and observe for agglutination.</li>
</ol>
<p>If agglutination is visible, quantitative estimation of the titer of the appropriate antibodies should be done</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="tube-agglutination-method">Tube agglutination method<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tube-agglutination-method" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Take a set of 8 clean dry test tubes for each serum to be tested.</li>
<li>Place 1.9ml of saline in tube 1 and 1 ml of saline in other tuber (2-8)</li>
<li>Transfer 0.1 ml of undiluted serum to tube 1. Mix thoroughly. The resultant dilution of serum is 1:20.</li>
<li>Further dilutions are done in the following</li>
</ol>
<p>a) Transfer 1ml of the diluted serum from tube 1 and place in tube 2 this leads to 1:40 dilutions in tube2
b) Repeat the transfer process for tube 7 after mixing.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>c) Leave 1 ml of saline in tube 8 at the 'saline control'</p>
<p>Note. Tube 1 has a serum dilution of 1:20, 1:40 (2), 1:80 (3), and 1:160 (4), 1:320 (5), 1:640 (6) &amp; 1:1280 (7).</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Add one drop of appropriate antigen in each (use only that antigen suspension which has given a positive reaction in the screening test).</li>
</ol>
<p>Note: Each antigen (O, H, AH, BH) will require a series of 8 tubes for determine the titer of their corresponding antibodies.</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>
<p>Mix well and incubate overnight (16-18 hrs) at 37°C.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Examine agglutination macroscopically.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Two tubes for positive control O and it antigen should be included.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="interpretation">Interpretation<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#interpretation" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Only a titer above 1:80 should be considered as significant.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A rise in titer (done each week) is considered to be definite evidence of infection. A single test result is considered of diagnostic value only when it is usually high (above 160).</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Antibiotic treatment in typhoid fever often prevents a rise in titer,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>A negative test does not rule out the possibility of infection because of the time when the blood sample was taken in relation to the stage of the disease.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ol start="5">
<li>Positive results should always be interpreted with reference to clinical findings.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-2-rickettsial-disease">9.2 Rickettsial Disease<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-2-rickettsial-disease" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rickettsiae resemble viruses in that they are obligate intercellular parasite and unable to survive as free-living organisms. They are about the size of the large viruses and can just be seen with the light microscope. Unlike viruses rickettsiae contain both RNA and DNA multiply by binary fission, they have cell wall that contains muramic acid and enzyme.</p>
<p>Based on their antigenic structure, the genus rickettsia has been divided into three main groups: typhus group (R. prowazeki, R. typhi), scrub typhus group (R. tsutsugamushi), spotted fever group (R.conori, R.siberica, R.rickettsi R.conoripijperi).</p>
<p>Man is an accidental host of rickettsia species except R. prowazeki; they live in intestinal tract of louse, fleas, ticks and mites. Reservoirs host include, dogs, rats, mice, rodents. Rickettsial disease can be acquired by inhaling of dried infected vector faces, through damaged skin bite of an infected vector ticks, mite, etc. The infection is characterized by high continuous fever, severe head ach and body pains,</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>marked weakness, enlarged spleen</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laboratory-diagnosis">Laboratory diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laboratory-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Embryonated egg inoculation technique used for culturing viruses can also be used for isolating rickettsiae however it require costly materials and performed in reference laboratory.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="serology">Serology<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#serology" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In rickettsial infection, specific IgM antibodies are produced followed by IgG response in the later stages. The most reliable and useful serological techniques to diagnose rickettsial infections are immunofluorescent assay and complement fixation test; however, this test is not available in district laboratory due to its cost</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="weil-felix-reaction">Weil-felix reaction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#weil-felix-reaction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>A Weil Felix test is a type of agglutination test most commonly used serologic test. The reaction is based on similarity of particular antigenic determinant, which occur in most species of pathogenic rickettsia and in the OX-19, OX -2 strains of Proteus vulgaris and OX-K strains of Proteus mirabilis. In other word, Proteus antigen is used to detect rickettsial antibody. This could be an example of hetrophile antigen antibody reaction. Weil Felix test has similar principle and procedure with Widal test.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Table 9.1 Weil-felix reactions in Rickettsial infection</p>
<table><thead><tr><th>Weil-Felix Reaction</th><th></th><th></th><th></th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Organisms</td><td>OX-19</td><td>OX-2</td><td>OX-K</td></tr><tr><td>TYPHUS GROUP</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>R.prowazeki</td><td>+++</td><td>+/-</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>R.typhi</td><td>+++</td><td>+/-</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>SCRUB TYPHUS TROUP</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>R.tsutsugamclshi</td><td>-</td><td>-</td><td>+++/-</td></tr><tr><td>SPOTTED FEVER GROUP</td><td></td><td></td><td></td></tr><tr><td>R. conori</td><td>+/++</td><td>+/++</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>R.conoripjperi</td><td>+/++</td><td>+/++</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>R.siberica</td><td>+/++</td><td>+/++</td><td>-</td></tr><tr><td>R.rickettsi</td><td>+/++</td><td>+/++</td><td>-</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>+++ frequent and large antibody response</p>
<ul>
<li>no antibody response</li>
</ul>
<p>Note: False negative reactions are common in scrub typhus.</p>
<p>False positive reactions may occur in Proteus infections, relapsing fever, brucellosis and other acute febrile illnesses.</p>
<p>A rise in titer in two consecutive specimen collected in interval is significant than a rise in titer in single specimen and a rise in titer in single specimen should not be taken as a positive sample.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="9-3-brucella-abortus">9.3 Brucella Abortus<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#9-3-brucella-abortus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Brucella aborts, gram-negative bacilli, is the causative microorganism of brucellosis. If it is a zoonoses that infect humans by accident. The agents of brucellosis are normal flora of the genital and urinary tract of many animals including pigs, cows, and dogs. Most human acquired brucellosis because of the ingestion of contaminated food products or through occupational exposure. Farmers, veterinarians, and slaughterhouse workers are particularly prone to infection.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="laboratory-diagnosis">Laboratory diagnosis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#laboratory-diagnosis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Because of the difficulty of isolating this organism by the culturing technique, many cases of brucellosis are diagnosed serologically by identifying the presence of antibodies. Antibodies usually appear within 2 to 3 weeks after infection. An antibody titer of 1:80 to 1:60 strongly suggests infection.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-questions">Review Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="say-true-or-false">Say true or false<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#say-true-or-false" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ol>
<li>Typhoid and paratyphoid fever can be diagnosed by Widal test</li>
<li>In well-felix test, some strains of Proteus vulugaris and proteus mirabilis antigen is utilized as reagent</li>
<li>Brucella abortus commonly affect human being.</li>
</ol>
