<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="quality-control">Quality control<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#quality-control" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Positive control-a prediluted serum containing at least 200  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">u</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{lu} / \mathrm{ml}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">lu</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">ml</span></span></span></span></span></span>  of ASO. This control should exhibit visible agglutination at the end of the 3-minute test period. Negative control serum a prediluted serum containing less than 100  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">u</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{lu} / \mathrm{ml}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">lu</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">ml</span></span></span></span></span></span>  of ASO. This control should exhibit a smooth or slightly granular appearance at the end of the 3-minute test period.</p>
<p>A positive and negative control should be tested and read concurrently with each group of patient sera.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Dilute the serum by saline in 1:2</li>
<li>Label the slide for positive control dilution negative control and patient sera</li>
<li>Pipette  <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>50</mn><mi>μ</mi><mi>l</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">50\mu l</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mord">50</span><span class="mord mathnormal">μ</span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.01968em;">l</span></span></span></span></span>  of the controls and patient sera onto the appropriately labeled cell (well)</li>
<li>Add one drop of latex reagent to each well</li>
<li>Mix the specimen with separate applicator stick spread the mixture evenly over the well.</li>
</ol>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ol start="6">
<li>Rotate the slide for exactly 3 minutes. Examine with a bright light</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reporting">Reporting<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reporting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Positive – agglutination</p>
<p>Negative – No agglutination</p>
<p>Agglutination demonstrates 200 lu/ml or more ASO. Positive results should be retested quantitatively.</p>
<p>A titer of 200 lu/ml or greater may be associated with rheumatic fever or glomerulonephritis.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="antistreptolysin-o-titration-kit">Antistreptolysin O titration kit<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#antistreptolysin-o-titration-kit" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>In the titration test, a constant amount of streptolysin O antigen reagent is added to a series of dilutions of the patient's serum. Following a period of incubation, Group O washed human or rabbit red cells are added. The tubes are then examined for lysis of the red cells. Haemolysis occurs in those tubes in which there is insufficient antibody to neutralize the antigen.</p>
<p>The highest dilution of serum showing no haemolysis is the ASO titer, the titer of ASO antibody in the serum is directly proportional to the reciprocal of the serum dilution. The antistreptolysin O titer is expressed in Todd units.</p>
<p>153</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-questions">Review Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rheumatoid-factor">RHEUMATOID FACTOR<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rheumatoid-factor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="learning-objective">Learning Objective<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#learning-objective" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="16-0-rheumatoid-factor">16.0. Rheumatoid Factor<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#16-0-rheumatoid-factor" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Rheumatoid factors are antibodies with specificity for antigen determinants on the Fc fragment of human or certain animal IgG. They're associated with IgG, IgM &amp; IgA. IgG &amp; IgM rheumatoid factors are the most common. During some disease of a joint, rheumatoid arthritis, an IgG antibody is produced following to its production the antibody become altered for unknown reason, against this altered antibody a second antibody (anti antibody) is produced which is known as antigammaglobulin antibody.</p>
<p>155</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="test-for-rheumatoid-arthritis">Test for Rheumatoid arthritis<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#test-for-rheumatoid-arthritis" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="rapid-latex-agglutination">Rapid latex agglutination<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rapid-latex-agglutination" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<p><strong>Principle:</strong> The test is based on the reaction between patient antibodies in the serum, known as the rheumatoid factor; and an antigen derived from gamma globulin. If rheumatoid factors are present in the serum, macroscopic agglutination will be visible when the latex reagent is mixed with the serum.</p>
<p><strong>Specimen:</strong> Serum</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="reagents-materials-required">Reagents &amp; materials required<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reagents-materials-required" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ul>
<li>Latex reagent</li>
<li>Glycine saline buffer</li>
<li>Capillary pipette</li>
<li>Applicator stick</li>
<li>Glass slide</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="additional-required-equipment">Additional required equipment<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#additional-required-equipment" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>

<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h3 level="3" id="procedure">Procedure<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#procedure" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h3></div>
<ol>
<li>Prepare 1:20 dilution of patient serum in glycine saline buffer (i.e. 0.1me of serum &amp; 1.9 me of diluent) and mix the tube contents</li>
</ol>
<p>156</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<ol start="2">
<li>Deliver one free falling drop of the diluted serum by using capillary pipette to one of the division of the slide.</li>
<li>Add one drop of positive control &amp; one drop of negative control to the appropriately labeled division of the slide</li>
<li>Mix the latex reagent &amp; add one drop to the patient specimen and to each of the controls.</li>
<li>Mix each specimen with a separate applicator stick over the entire area of there respective divisions on the slide</li>
<li>Tilt the slide back and forty, slowly and evenly, for 2 minutes</li>
<li>Observe for macroscopic agglutination using a direct light source.</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="reporting-results">Reporting results<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#reporting-results" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Positive reaction: agglutination of the latex suspension indicates the presence of rheumatoid factor in the specimen.</p>
<p>Negative reaction: absence of visible agglutination.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="review-questions">Review Questions<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#review-questions" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>Discuss how the rheumatoid factor is produced in the body.</li>
</ol>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-acc0fb7d.jpeg" alt="img-30.jpeg"></p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="glossary">Glossary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glossary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<p>Active immunity: Protection acquired by deliberate introduction of Performed antibody or immune cells into a non-immune host.</p>
<p>Antibody: Secreted immunoglobulin protein, particularly those that can bind specifically to a given antigen.</p>
<p>Antigen: A substance that reacts with antibodies or T-cell receptors.</p>
<p>Antiserum: Serum containing antibodies raised against a specific antigen</p>
<p>Antitoxin: Protective antibodies that inactivate soluble toxic protein products.</p>
<p>Autoimmunity: Immunity to self-antigens.</p>
<p>Bursa of Fabricius: The hindgut organ located in the cloaca of birds that controls the ontogeny of B-lymphocytes</p>
<p>Bursa equivalent: The hypothetical organ or organs analogous to the bursa of Fabricius in non-avian species</p>
<p>Cardiolipin: A substance derived from beef heart, probably a component of mitochondria membranes that serves as an antigenic substrate for reagin or antitreponemal antibody.</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Cell mediated immunity: immunity in which the participation of lymphocytes and macrophages is predominant</p>
<p>Clone: A group of cells all of which are the progeny of single cells</p>
<p>Complement: A system of serum proteins that can be induced to carry out a cascade of enzymatic reactions which may lead to lysis of foreign cells and to formation of certain opsonins and inflammatory mediators.</p>
<p>C- reactive protein: An antibacterial serum protein that binds pneumococcal C-protein.</p>
<p>Cytokine: Any of a group of soluble polypeptide mediators that regulates cellular growth or function.</p>
<p>Effector cell: Any cell that actively carries out an immunologic attack.</p>
<p>Hapten: A substance that is not immunogenic but can react with an antibody of appropriate specificity.</p>
<p>Lymphocytes: A mononuclear cells 7-12mm in diameter containing a nucleus with densely packed chromatin and small rim of cytoplasm.</p>
<p>Lymphokine: Any cytokine produced by lymphoid cell.</p>
<p>160</p>
<p>Immunology and Serology</p>
<p>Thymus: A primary lymphoid organ situated in the anterior mediastinum which is required for and is the site of lymphopoiesis.</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251221-acc0fb7d.jpeg" alt="img-31.jpeg"></p>
